=== Example 0 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance and Baroque music.
Any choral conductor is a musician.
Some musicians love music.
Miroslav Venhoda published a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda was a Czech choral conductor who specialized in the performance of Renaissance and Baroque music.
FOL: ChoralConductor(MiroslavVenhoda) & SpecializesIn(MiroslavVenhoda, RenaissancePerformance) & SpecializesIn(MiroslavVenhoda, BaroquePerformance)
TEXT: Any choral conductor is a musician.
FOL: all x. (ChoralConductor(x) -> Musician(x))
TEXT: Some musicians love music.
FOL: exists x. (Musician(x) & Loves(x, Music))
TEXT: Miroslav Venhoda published a book in 1946 called Method of Studying Gregorian Chant.
FOL: Published(MiroslavVenhoda, "Method of Studying Gregorian Chant", 1946)
TEXT: No choral conductor specialized in the performance of Renaissance.
FOL: -exists x. (ChoralConductor(x) & SpecializesIn(x, RenaissancePerformance))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
Given the first premise, we know that Miroslav Venhoda specialized in Renaissance and Baroque music. Therefore, there does exist at least one choral conductor who specializes in Renaissance performance, which directly contradicts the conclusion. Thus, the conclusion does not logically follow from the premises, and the correct evaluation is False.
Processed: False

Reference: False
========================================

=== Example 1 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Some fish stings people.
Stonefish is a fish.
Stonefish stings when stepped on.
If a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death to them.
To treat stonefish stings, apply heat to the affected area or use an antivenom.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Stings of some fish can cause death if not treated.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Some fish stings people.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x))

TEXT: Stonefish is a fish.
FOL: Fish(Stonefish)

TEXT: Stonefish stings when stepped on.
FOL: StingsWhenSteppedOn(Stonefish)

TEXT: If a stonefish stings someone and they are not treated, it can cause death to them.
FOL: all x. (Stings(Stonefish, x) & -Treated(x) -> Death(x))

TEXT: To treat stonefish stings, apply heat to the affected area or use an antivenom.
FOL: all x. (Stings(Stonefish, x) -> Treat(x, Heat | Antivenom))

TEXT: Stings of some fish can cause death if not treated.
FOL: exists x. (Fish(x) & Stings(x, y) & -Treated(y) -> Death(y))

ANSWER: True

Explanation: From the premises, we know that Stonefish is a type of fish that stings people when stepped on and if not treated can cause death. Since Stonefish is a specific instance of fish that can cause death if its sting is untreated, it's reasonable to conclude that stings of some fish (including stonefish) can indeed cause death if not treated.
Processed: True

Reference: True
========================================

</PREMISES>

</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: exists x. (Bear(x) & BearInZoo(x))
TEXT: Not all bears are wild.
FOL: -all x. (Bear(x) -> Wild(x))

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
Given the premises, we know that there exist bears in zoos, and all bears in zoos are not wild. Therefore, at least those specific bears in zoos are not wild. Hence, it cannot be true that all bears are wild, proving the conclusion correct.
Processed: True

TEXT:

FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No reptile has fur.
All snakes are reptiles.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Some snake has fur.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: No reptile has fur.
FOL: all x. (Reptile(x) -> -HasFur(x))
TEXT: All snakes are reptiles.
FOL: all x. (Snake(x) -> Reptile(x))
TEXT: Some snake has fur.
FOL: exists x. (Snake(x) & HasFur(x))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
From the premises, we know that for any entity \(x\), if \(x\) is a snake, then \(x\) must be a reptile. Additionally, no reptile has fur. Therefore, if an entity is a snake, it cannot have fur since all snakes are reptiles and no reptile has fur. Thus, the conclusion that "some snake has fur" is false according to the given premises.
Processed: False

Reference: False

=== Example 4 ===

TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.

TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Ambiortus is a prehistoric bird genus.
Ambiortus Dementjevi is the only known species of Ambiortus.
Mongolia was where Ambiortus Dementjevi lived.
Yevgeny Kurochkin was the discoverer of Ambiortus.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Yevgeny Kurochkin discovered a new bird genus.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Ambiortus is a prehistoric bird genus.
FOL: PrehistoricBirdGenus(Ambiortus)
TEXT: Ambiortus Dementjevi is the only known species of Ambiortus.
FOL: all x. (SpeciesOf(x, Ambiortus) <-> x = AmbiortusDementjevi)
TEXT: Mongolia was where Ambiortus Dementjevi lived.
FOL: LivedIn(AmbiortusDementjevi, Mongolia)
TEXT: Yevgeny Kurochkin was the discoverer of Ambiortus.
FOL: Discoverer(Ambiortus, YevgenyKurochkin)
TEXT: Yevgeny Kurochkin discovered a new bird genus.
FOL: Exists x. (PrehistoricBirdGenus(x) & Discoverer(x, YevgenyKurochkin))

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
Given that Yevgeny Kurochkin was the discoverer of Ambiortus and Ambiortus is a prehistoric bird genus, we can conclude that Yevgeny Kurochkin indeed discovered a new bird genus (Ambiortus). Therefore, the conclusion logically follows from the premises.

=== Example 5 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.

TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: LocatedIn(FortCarillon, NewFrance)
TEXT: New France is not in Europe.
FOL: -LocatedIn(NewFrance, Europe)
TEXT: Pierre de Rigaud de Vaudreuil built a fort in New France.
FOL: Exists x. (BuiltBy(PierreDeRigaudDeVaudreuil, x) & LocatedIn(x, NewFrance))

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
From the premises, we know that Fort Carillon (which is the same as Fort Ticonderoga) was built by Pierre de Rigaud de Vaudreuil and that it was located in New France. Hence, it can be concluded that Pierre de Rigaud de Vaudreuil indeed built a fort (Fort Carillon/Fort Ticonderoga) in New France. Therefore, the conclusion logically follows from the premises.
Processed: True

TEXT: A highly developed city is located in the western hemisphere of the earth.

ANSWER: Uncertain

All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Westworld is an American science fiction-thriller TV series.
In 2016, a television series named Westworld debuted on HBO.
The TV series Westworld is adapted from the original film in 1973, which was written and directed by Michael Crichton.
The 1973 film Westworld is about robots that malfunction and begin killing human visitors.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Michael Crichton has directed a film about malfunctioning robots.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Westworld is an American science fiction-thriller TV series.
FOL: Westworld(TVSeries) & American(TVSeries) & ScienceFiction(TVSeries) & Thriller(TVSeries)

TEXT: In 2016, a television series named Westworld debuted on HBO.
FOL: Debut(Westworld, 2016, HBO)

TEXT: The TV series Westworld is adapted from the original film in 1973, which was written and directed by Michael Crichton.
FOL: AdaptedFrom(WestworldTV, WestworldFilm1973) & WrittenBy(WestworldFilm1973, MichaelCrichton) & DirectedBy(WestworldFilm1973, MichaelCrichton)

TEXT: The 1973 film Westworld is about robots that malfunction and begin killing human visitors.
FOL: Topic(WestworldFilm1973, MalfunctioningRobotsKillingHumans)

TEXT: Michael Crichton has directed a film about malfunctioning robots.
FOL: DirectedBy(MichaelCrichton, FilmAboutMalfunctioningRobots)

ANSWER: True

Explanation: From the given premises, we know that "The TV series Westworld is adapted from the original film in 1973, which was written and directed by Michael Crichton" (DirectedBy(WestworldFilm1973, MichaelCrichton)) and that "The 1973 film Westworld is about robots that malfunction and begin killing human visitors" (Topic(WestworldFilm1973, MalfunctioningRobotsKillingHumans)). These statements together imply that Michael Crichton has indeed directed a film about malfunctioning robots, making the conclusion true.
Processed: True

Reference: True

=== Example 9 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (ProfessionalAthlete(x) -> SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))
TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Xiufeng, Xiangshan, Diecai, Qixing are districts in the city of Guilin.
Yangshuo is not a district in Guilin.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Xiangshan and Diecai are districts in the same city.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Xiufeng, Xiangshan, Diecai, Qixing are districts in the city of Guilin.
FOL: DistrictInCity(Xiufeng, Guilin) & DistrictInCity(Xiangshan, Guilin) & DistrictInCity(Diecai, Guilin) & DistrictInCity(Qixing, Guilin)
TEXT: Yangshuo is not a district in Guilin.
FOL: -DistrictInCity(Yangshuo, Guilin)
TEXT: Xiangshan and Diecai are districts in the same city.
FOL: SameCity(District(Xiangshan), District(Diecai))

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
Given the premises, we know that Xiangshan and Diecai are both districts in Guilin. Since they are both specified to be districts within the same city (Guilin), the statement that "Xiangshan and Diecai are districts in the same city" follows directly from the premises. Therefore, the answer is True.
Processed: True

Reference: True

Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.

The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.

FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.

TEXT: All paper is woodware.

TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))

FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

</EVALUATE>

ANSWER: False

<PREMISES>
The only types of mammals that lay eggs are either platypuses or echidnas.
Platypuses are not hyrax.
Echidnas are not hyrax.
No mammals are invertebrates.
All animals are either vertebrates or invertebrates.
Mammals are animals.
Hyraxes are mammals.
Grebes lay eggs.
Grebes are not platypuses and also not echidnas.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Hyraxes lay eggs.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: The only types of mammals that lay eggs are either platypuses or echidnas.
FOL: all x. (Mammal(x) & LaysEggs(x) -> (Platypus(x) | Echidna(x)))
TEXT: Platypuses are not hyrax.
FOL: all x. (Platypus(x) -> -Hyrax(x))
TEXT: Echidnas are not hyrax.
FOL: all x. (Echidna(x) -> -Hyrax(x))
TEXT: No mammals are invertebrates.
FOL: all x. (Mammal(x) -> -Invertebrate(x))
TEXT: All animals are either vertebrates or invertebrates.
FOL: all x. (Animal(x) -> (Vertebrate(x) | Invertebrate(x)))
TEXT: Mammals are animals.
FOL: all x. (Mammal(x) -> Animal(x))
TEXT: Hyraxes are mammals.
FOL: all x. (Hyrax(x) -> Mammal(x))
TEXT: Grebes lay eggs.
FOL: LaysEggs(Grebe)
TEXT: Grebes are not platypuses and also not echidnas.
FOL: -Platypus(Grebe) & -Echidna(Grebe)
TEXT: Hyraxes lay eggs.
FOL: LaysEggs(Hyrax)

ANSWER: False

Explanation: Given the premise "The only types of mammals that lay eggs are either platypuses or echidnas," and knowing that "Hyraxes are mammals" but "Hyraxes are not platypuses and not echidnas," it logically follows that hyraxes do not lay eggs since they don't belong to the only two mammalian groups known to lay eggs. Therefore, the conclusion that "Hyraxes lay eggs" is false based on the given premises.
Processed: False

</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:

FOL: AmericanScreenwriter(MaggieFriedman) & Producer(MaggieFriedman)
TEXT: Maggie Friedman was the showrunner and executive producer of the lifetime television series Witches of East End.
FOL: Showrunner(MaggieFriedman, WitchesOfEastEnd) & ExecutiveProducer(MaggieFriedman, WitchesOfEastEnd)
TEXT: Witches of East End is a fantasy-drama series.
FOL: FantasyDramaSeries(WitchesOfEastEnd)
TEXT: Maggie Friedman produced and developed Eastwick.
FOL: Produced(MaggieFriedman, Eastwick) & Developed(MaggieFriedman, Eastwick)
TEXT: Eastwick is a series by ABC.
FOL: SeriesByABC(Eastwick)
TEXT: There is a series by ABC that was developed by the showrunner of Witches of East End.
FOL: exists x. (SeriesByABC(x) & Developed(Showrunner(WitchesOfEastEnd), x))

ANSWER: True

Additionally, "Eastwick" is a series by ABC (SeriesByABC(Eastwick)). Therefore, "Eastwick", which is a series by ABC, was indeed developed by Maggie Friedman who was also the showrunner of "Witches of East End". Thus, the conclusion follows from the premises.
Processed: True

Boney M. had several German #1 singles.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
"Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!" peaked below #1 on the German charts.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

TEXT: Boney M. had several German #1 singles.

TEXT: "Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!" was a big hit all over Europe.
FOL: BigHit("Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!", Europe)
TEXT: "Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!" was not in German #1 singles.
FOL: -GermanCharts("Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!", 1)
TEXT: A song that peaks below #1 on the german charts is also a song that is not the #1 single in Germany.
FOL: all x. (Song(x) & PeakedBelowOneGermanCharts(x) -> -GermanCharts(x, 1))

TEXT: "Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!" peaked below #1 on the German charts.
FOL: PeakedBelowOneGermanCharts("Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!")

ANSWER: Uncertain

Explanation:
- From the premises, we know that "Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!" was not a German #1 single, but this alone does not provide enough information to determine its exact position on the German charts.
- The premise states that any song that peaked below #1 on the German charts is not a German #1 single, which aligns with what we know about the song's status on the chart.
- However, without specific information about the peak position of "Hooray! Hooray! It's a Holi-Holiday!" on the German charts, we cannot conclusively say it peaked below #1.
- Therefore, based solely on the provided information, the conclusion cannot be definitively confirmed or denied.
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: True

Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.

If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>

<EVALUATE>

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

FOL: Develops(ETS, AssessmentsK12Statewide) & UsedFor(AssessmentsK12Statewide, AccountabilityTesting) & InStates(AssessmentsK12Statewide, ManyStates)
TEXT: ETS develops assessments for K-12 statewide as well as entry to US tertiary and quaternary education institutions.
FOL: Develops(ETS, AssessmentsK12Statewide) & Develops(ETS, AssessmentsEntryUSEducation)

ANSWER: True

Explanation: Based on the premises, we know that ETS develops assessments for K-12 statewide (from the fourth premise) and also develops assessments associated with entry to US tertiary and quaternary education institutions (from the third premise). TEXT: Water from the Croton River watershed flows to somewhere in New York.
FOL: exists x. (PartOf(x, NewYork) & FlowsTo(WaterFrom(DrainageBasin(CrotonRiver)), x))

ANSWER: True

<PREMISES>
Six, seven and eight are real numbers.
If a real number equals another real number added by one, the first number is larger.
If the number x is larger than the number y, then y is not larger than x.
Seven equals six plus one.
Eight equals seven plus one.
Two is positive.
If a number is positive, then the double of it is also positive.
Eight is the double of four.
Four is the double of two.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Eight is larger than seven.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Six, seven and eight are real numbers.
FOL: RealNumber(Six) & RealNumber(Seven) & RealNumber(Eight)
TEXT: If a real number equals another real number added by one, the first number is larger.
FOL: all x. all y. (RealNumber(x) & RealNumber(y) & Equal(x, Plus(y, One)) -> Larger(x, y))
TEXT: If the number x is larger than the number y, then y is not larger than x.
FOL: all x. all y. (Larger(x, y) -> -Larger(y, x))
TEXT: Seven equals six plus one.
FOL: Equal(Seven, Plus(Six, One))
TEXT: Eight equals seven plus one.
FOL: Equal(Eight, Plus(Seven, One))
TEXT: Two is positive.
FOL: Positive(Two)
TEXT: If a number is positive, then the double of it is also positive.
FOL: all x. (Positive(x) -> Positive(Double(x)))
TEXT: Eight is the double of four.
FOL: Equal(Eight, Double(Four))
TEXT: Four is the double of two.
FOL: Equal(Four, Double(Two))
TEXT: Eight is larger than seven.
FOL: Larger(Eight, Seven)

ANSWER: True

Explanation: Given that "Seven equals six plus one" and "Eight equals seven plus one", we can infer from the premise "If a real number equals another real number added by one, the first number is larger" that Seven is larger than Six and Eight is larger than Seven. Hence, the conclusion that "Eight is larger than seven" is directly supported by the given premises.

Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>

All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.

TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.

FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Six, seven and eight are real numbers.
If a real number equals another real number added by one, the first number is larger.
If the number x is larger than the number y, then y is not larger than x.
Seven equals six plus one.
Eight equals seven plus one.
Two is positive.
If a number is positive, then the double of it is also positive.
Eight is the double of four.
Four is the double of two.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Eight is positive.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Six, seven and eight are real numbers.
FOL: RealNumber(Six) & RealNumber(Seven) & RealNumber(Eight)

TEXT: If a real number equals another real number added by one, the first number is larger.
FOL: all x. all y. (RealNumber(x) & RealNumber(y) & Equal(x, Add(y, One)) -> Larger(x, y))

TEXT: If the number x is larger than the number y, then y is not larger than x.
FOL: all x. all y. (Larger(x, y) -> -Larger(y, x))

TEXT: Seven equals six plus one.
FOL: Equal(Seven, Add(Six, One))

TEXT: Eight equals seven plus one.
FOL: Equal(Eight, Add(Seven, One))

TEXT: Two is positive.
FOL: Positive(Two)

TEXT: If a number is positive, then the double of it is also positive.
FOL: all x. (Positive(x) -> Positive(Multiply(x, Two)))

TEXT: Eight is the double of four.
FOL: Equal(Eight, Multiply(Four, Two))

TEXT: Four is the double of two.
FOL: Equal(Four, Multiply(Two, Two))

TEXT: Eight is positive.
FOL: Positive(Eight)

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
- From "Equal(Four, Multiply(Two, Two))" and "Positive(Two)", we infer that "Positive(Four)" is true because "Positive(x) -> Positive(Multiply(x, Two))".
- From "Equal(Eight, Multiply(Four, Two))" and "Positive(Four)", we infer that "Positive(Eight)" is true using the same rule.

Thus, the conclusion "Eight is positive" logically follows from the premises.
Processed: True

Reference: True

Generation 1:
TEXT: All volunteers receive intangible benefits for their work.
FOL: all x. (Volunteer(x) -> IntangibleBenefits(x))
TEXT: Volunteers work regularly or on an as-needed basis.
FOL: all x. (Volunteer(x) -> (RegularlyWorks(x) | AsNeededBasis(x)))
TEXT: Some volunteers are trained.
FOL: exists x. (Volunteer(x) & Trained(x))
TEXT: Volunteers work in groups or individually.
FOL: all x. (Volunteer(x) -> (WorksInGroups(x) | WorksIndividually(x)))
TEXT: Environmental volunteers contribute toward environmental management or conservation.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentalVolunteer(x) -> (ContributesToManagement(x) | ContributesToConservation(x)))
TEXT: Participating in natural disaster response is an example of volunteers working in groups on an as-needed basis.
FOL: all x. (NaturalDisasterResponse(x) -> (WorksInGroups(x) & AsNeededBasis(x)))
TEXT: Volunteers who participate in natural disaster response receive intangible benefits for their work.
FOL: all x. (NaturalDisasterResponse(x) -> IntangibleBenefits(x))

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
From the premise "all x. (Volunteer(x) -> IntangibleBenefits(x))", we know that every volunteer receives intangible benefits.
From the premise "all x. (NaturalDisasterResponse(x) -> (WorksInGroups(x) & AsNeededBasis(x)))" and the fact that participating in natural disaster response is an example of volunteering, we can infer that those who participate in natural disaster response are volunteers.
Thus, since all volunteers receive intangible benefits, it follows that volunteers who participate in natural disaster response also receive intangible benefits.
Processed: True

Reference: True

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))

TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.

FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

TEXT: All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
FOL: all x. (OlympicGoldMedalWinner(x) -> ProfessionalAthlete(x))

FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
All important scientific achievements are U.S. inventions.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:

ANSWER: False

Explanation: The second premise states that some artificial satellites are not U.S. inventions. Since all artificial satellites are important scientific achievements (first premise), this means there exist important scientific achievements that are not U.S. inventions. Therefore, the conclusion that all important scientific achievements are U.S. inventions cannot be true.

TEXT: No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
FOL: all x. (FullTimeScientist(x) -> -SpendOn(x, MostOfTheirTime, Sports))
TEXT: All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
FOL: all x. (NobelPhysicsLaureate(x) -> FullTimeScientist(x))
TEXT: Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: SpendOn(Amy, MostOfTheirTime, Sports) | OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
FOL: -NobelPhysicsLaureate(Amy) -> -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy)
TEXT: If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
FOL: -OlympicGoldMedalWinner(Amy) -> NobelLaureate(Amy)

ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
TOra is a GUI.
GUIs are software.
Software can be free or paid.
Paid Software is not under the GNU General Public License.
TOra is under the GNU General Public License.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
TOra is a free software.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: TOra is a GUI.
FOL: GUI(TOra)
TEXT: GUIs are software.
FOL: all x. (GUI(x) -> Software(x))
TEXT: Software can be free or paid.
FOL: all x. (Software(x) -> (Free(x) | Paid(x)))
TEXT: Paid Software is not under the GNU General Public License.
FOL: all x. (Paid(x) -> -GPL(x))
TEXT: TOra is under the GNU General Public License.
FOL: GPL(TOra)
TEXT: TOra is a free software.
FOL: Free(TOra)

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
From the premises:
1. GUI(TOra)
2. all x. (GUI(x) -> Software(x)) implies Software(TOra).
3. all x. (Software(x) -> (Free(x) | Paid(x))) implies (Free(TOra) | Paid(TOra)).
4. all x. (Paid(x) -> -GPL(x)), so Paid(TOra) would imply -GPL(TOra), but we know GPL(TOra) from premise 5, therefore -Paid(TOra).
5. GPL(TOra).

Given that TOra is under the GNU General Public License and paid software cannot be under this license, it implies that TOra cannot be paid. Therefore, since TOra must either be free or paid, and we have established it is not paid, TOra must be free. Thus, the conclusion that TOra is a free software is true based on the given premises.
Processed: True

Reference: True

<PREMISES>
Ainderby Quernhow is a village and civil parish in the Hambleton District.
Hambleton District is in North Yorkshire.
North Yorkshire is in England.
If place A is located in place B and place B is located in place C, then place A is located in place C.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
There is a village in England.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Ainderby Quernhow is a village and civil parish in the Hambleton District.
FOL: Village(AinderbyQuernhow) & CivilParish(AinderbyQuernhow) & LocatedIn(AinderbyQuernhow, HambletonDistrict)
TEXT: Hambleton District is in North Yorkshire.
FOL: LocatedIn(HambletonDistrict, NorthYorkshire)
TEXT: North Yorkshire is in England.
FOL: LocatedIn(NorthYorkshire, England)
TEXT: If place A is located in place B and place B is located in place C, then place A is located in place C.
FOL: all A. all B. all C. (LocatedIn(A, B) & LocatedIn(B, C) -> LocatedIn(A, C))
TEXT: There is a village in England.
FOL: exists V. (Village(V) & LocatedIn(V, England))

ANSWER: True

Explanation:
From the premises, we can derive that Ainderby Quernhow is a village (Village(AinderbyQuernhow)). We also know it is located within the Hambleton District, which is in North Yorkshire, and North Yorkshire is in England. Given the transitive relation provided by the fourth premise (if A is in B and B is in C, then A is in C), we can infer that Ainderby Quernhow is located in England. Therefore, since Ainderby Quernhow is a village and is located in England, the conclusion that "there is a village in England" follows directly from the premises.
Processed: True

Therefore, the conclusion "Douglas Adams is a writer" follows from the premises.

<EVALUATE>

Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>

ANSWER: False

<PREMISES>
If two soccer teams score the same number of goals in one UCL final during the regular time, they need to play for the extra time.
If two soccer teams score the same number of goals in one UCL final during both regular and extra time, they need to play the penalty shoot-out.
Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored one goal in the 2016 UCL final during the regular time.
Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored zero goals in the 2016 UCL final during the extra time.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid needed to play a penalty shoot-out in the 2016 UCL final.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: If two soccer teams score the same number of goals in one UCL final during the regular time, they need to play for the extra time.
FOL: all x. all y. (SoccerTeams(x, y) & UCLFinal(x, y) & SameGoalsRegularTime(x, y) -> NeedExtraTime(x, y))
TEXT: If two soccer teams score the same number of goals in one UCL final during both regular and extra time, they need to play the penalty shoot-out.
FOL: all x. all y. (SoccerTeams(x, y) & UCLFinal(x, y) & SameGoalsRegularTime(x, y) & SameGoalsExtraTime(x, y) -> NeedPenaltyShootOut(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored one goal in the 2016 UCL final during the regular time.
FOL: SameGoalsRegularTime(RealMadrid, AtleticoMadrid) & UCLFinal(RealMadrid, AtleticoMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored zero goals in the 2016 UCL final during the extra time.
FOL: SameGoalsExtraTime(RealMadrid, AtleticoMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid needed to play a penalty shoot-out in the 2016 UCL final.
FOL: NeedPenaltyShootOut(RealMadrid, AtleticoMadrid)

ANSWER: True

Explanation: According to the premises, since Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid had the same number of goals both during regular and extra times in the 2016 UCL final, they needed to proceed to the penalty shoot-out as per the second premise. Therefore, the conclusion follows logically from the premises provided.
Processed: True

<PREMISES>
If two soccer teams score the same number of goals in one UCL final during the regular time, they need to play for the extra time.
If two soccer teams score the same number of goals in one UCL final during both regular and extra time, they need to play the penalty shoot-out.
Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored one goal in the 2016 UCL final during the regular time.
Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored zero goals in the 2016 UCL final during the extra time.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid did not need to play a penalty shoot-out in the 2016 UCL final.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: If two soccer teams score the same number of goals in one UCL final during the regular time, they need to play for the extra time.
FOL: all x. all y. (SoccerTeams(x, y) & UCLFinal(x, y) & ScoreSameGoals(x, y, RegularTime) -> NeedExtraTime(x, y))
TEXT: If two soccer teams score the same number of goals in one UCL final during both regular and extra time, they need to play the penalty shoot-out.
FOL: all x. all y. (SoccerTeams(x, y) & UCLFinal(x, y) & ScoreSameGoals(x, y, RegularTime) & ScoreSameGoals(x, y, ExtraTime) -> NeedPenaltyShootOut(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored one goal in the 2016 UCL final during the regular time.
FOL: ScoreSameGoals(RealMadrid, AtleticoMadrid, RegularTime) & UCLFinal(RealMadrid, AtleticoMadrid) & Year(2016)
TEXT: Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored zero goals in the 2016 UCL final during the extra time.
FOL: ScoreSameGoals(RealMadrid, AtleticoMadrid, ExtraTime)
TEXT: Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid did not need to play a penalty shoot-out in the 2016 UCL final.
FOL: -NeedPenaltyShootOut(RealMadrid, AtleticoMadrid)

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
From the premises, we can infer that since Real Madrid and Atltico Madrid both scored the same number of goals (one goal each) during regular time, they needed to play extra time according to the first premise. Additionally, they both scored zero goals in the extra time, meaning they still had the same number of goals at the end of the extra time. Based on the second premise, this means they would need to play a penalty shoot-out. Therefore, the conclusion that they did not need to play a penalty shoot-out is false.
Processed: False

</EVALUATE>

Ableton makes music software.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Ableton does not have an office in Germany.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

FOL: HasOffice(Ableton, Germany)

FOL: HasOffice(Ableton, USA)

FOL: DifferentCountries(USA, Germany)
TEXT: Any company that has offices in different countries is a multinational company.

TEXT: Ableton does not have an office in Germany.
FOL: -HasOffice(Ableton, Germany)

=== Example 42 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.
FOL: all x. (Paper(x) -> Woodware(x))
TEXT: Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.
FOL: all x. (EnvironmentFriendly(x) -> Good(x))
TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.

If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.

<PREMISES>
China is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
If someone is from China, then they are from a country of BRICS.
India is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
If someone is from India, then they are in a country of BRICS.
All people from China are Chinese people.
All people from India are Indian people.
There is a person from India.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
No people from BRICS are Indian people.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: China is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
FOL: BRICS(China) & EmergingEconomy(China)
TEXT: If someone is from China, then they are from a country of BRICS.
FOL: all x. (FromChina(x) -> FromBRICS(x))
TEXT: India is one of the BRICS, and its economy is emerging.
FOL: BRICS(India) & EmergingEconomy(India)
TEXT: If someone is from India, then they are in a country of BRICS.
FOL: all x. (FromIndia(x) -> FromBRICS(x))
TEXT: All people from China are Chinese people.
FOL: all x. (FromChina(x) -> Chinese(x))
TEXT: All people from India are Indian people.
FOL: all x. (FromIndia(x) -> Indian(x))
TEXT: There is a person from India.
FOL: exists x. FromIndia(x)
TEXT: No people from BRICS are Indian people.
FOL: -(exists x. (FromBRICS(x) & Indian(x)))

ANSWER: False

Explanation:
Given that India is part of BRICS (from the premise "India is one of the BRICS"), and we know there exists a person from India (from the premise "There is a person from India"), any person from India is both from a BRICS country (due to the premise "If someone is from India, then they are in a country of BRICS") and Indian (from the premise "All people from India are Indian people"). Therefore, the statement "No people from BRICS are Indian people" is false because we can infer the existence of at least one person who is from BRICS and is Indian.
Processed: False

Reference: False

Cristiano Ronaldo is a soccer player.
Cristiano Ronaldo can use his right foot very efficiently.
Cristiano Ronaldo has scored many goals using his left foot.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Cristiano Ronaldo is a top soccer player.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
TEXT: Soccer players have a right foot and a left foot.
FOL: all x. (SoccerPlayer(x) -> HasFoot(x, Right) & HasFoot(x, Left))

TEXT: Top soccer players are soccer players who can use both the left foot and right foot very efficiently.
FOL: all x. (TopSoccerPlayer(x) <-> SoccerPlayer(x) & UseEfficiently(x, Left) & UseEfficiently(x, Right))

TEXT: If a soccer player can score many goals using the left foot, they can use that foot very efficiently.
FOL: all x. (SoccerPlayer(x) & ScoreManyGoals(x, Left) -> UseEfficiently(x, Left))

TEXT: If a soccer player can score many goals using the right foot, they can use that foot very efficiently.
FOL: all x. (SoccerPlayer(x) & ScoreManyGoals(x, Right) -> UseEfficiently(x, Right))

TEXT: Cristiano Ronaldo is a soccer player.
FOL: SoccerPlayer(CristianoRonaldo)

TEXT: Cristiano Ronaldo can use his right foot very efficiently.
FOL: UseEfficiently(CristianoRonaldo, Right)

TEXT: Cristiano Ronaldo has scored many goals using his left foot.
FOL: ScoreManyGoals(CristianoRonaldo, Left)

TEXT: Cristiano Ronaldo is a top soccer player.
FOL: TopSoccerPlayer(CristianoRonaldo)

ANSWER: True

Explanation: From the premises, we know Cristiano Ronaldo is a soccer player who can use his right foot very efficiently and has scored many goals with his left foot. Given the rule that scoring many goals with a foot implies efficient usage of that foot, we can conclude that Cristiano Ronaldo uses his left foot very efficiently as well. Since he meets the condition of being able to use both feet very efficiently, according to the definition provided for top soccer players, Cristiano Ronaldo is indeed a top soccer player.
Processed: True

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to translate each of the premises and conclusions into FOL expressions.and then to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises. The output should follow format TEXT: 
FOL: 
TEXT: 
FOL:... ANSWER: 


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
FOL: all x. (Biodegradable(x) -> EnvironmentFriendly(x))
TEXT: All woodware is biodegradable.
FOL: all x. (Woodware(x) -> Biodegradable(x))
TEXT: All paper is woodware.

FOL: -(exists x. (Good(x) & Bad(x)))
TEXT: All environment-friendly things are good.

TEXT: A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
FOL: ((Paper(Worksheet) & -EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)) | (-Paper(Worksheet) & EnvironmentFriendly(Worksheet)))
TEXT: A worksheet is not biodegradable.
FOL: -Dispensable(Worksheet)

ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
TEXT: A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & MorePoints(x, y) -> RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
FOL: all x. all y. (LaLigaSoccerTeam(x) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(y) & -MorePoints(x, y) & -MorePoints(y, x) & MorePointsInGameBetween(x, y) ->  RankHigherThan(x, y))
TEXT: Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
FOL: LaLigaSoccerTeam(RealMadrid) & LaLigaSoccerTeam(Barcelona)
TEXT: Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
FOL: MorePoints(RealMadrid, Barcelona)
TEXT: Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
FOL: -MorePointsInGameBetween(RealMadrid, Barcelona) & -MorePointsInGameBetween(Barcelona, RealMadrid)
TEXT: Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
FOL: HigherRank(RealMadrid, Barcelona)

ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
